[1] Prologue
[2] It was January 1st, the day after the Lunar New Year's Eve.
[3] Daozhu woke up at 7 am, determined to sleep until the sun was high in the sky. He had drunk heavily the night before, and the alcohol was still coursing through his veins, but he couldn't muster the desire to sleep in. So, he crawled out of bed.
[4] His wife was still asleep beside him, pulling the cotton blanket over her head. Her long, seaweed-like hair spilled out from under the pillow. Daozhu was tempted to return to bed, but he resisted the urge.
[5] Daozhu wondered why he was even getting up. He had no pressing matters to attend to, and his friends wouldn't arrive until the afternoon. It was New Year's Day, and he didn't have to go to work.
[6] There should have been nothing to disturb Daozhu's sleep, but he felt as though he had been forced to wake up.
[7] Daozhu pulled back the curtains, and the sky matched his mood, shrouded in a thin layer of clouds. He finally understood. The feeling of his body being manipulated by an unseen hand was a "premonition."
[8] Daozhu added a sweater over his woolen shirt and opened the window. It was then that he realized it had snowed while he was asleep. The flower beds and garden stones were covered in a white blanket.
[9] Daozhu had gone to bed early the night before, not wanting to stay up watching TV with his wife. He regretted not staying up a bit longer to enjoy the snowfall and have a drink. The thought of such a winter activity seemed to force his mind to focus on something more festive, while also distracting him from other thoughts.
[10] Daozhu walked out to the garden, his breath forming a cloud of white mist. It melted away as he exhaled, and he could see the neighbor's cherry tree in the distance.
[11] Although the snowfall was not as heavy as in previous years, the New Year's Day did snow, giving a bit of a winter feel; when he came into contact with the outside air, his body almost froze. The weather has been quite unusual lately, and the cherry buds that prematurely sprouted due to the warm winter seem to be swelling up, eager to shake off the scant snow.
[12] The "premonition" deepened in a worse form, and the cherry buds seemed like an ominous omen.
[13] It has been two years...
[14] Yutao stood motionless in the courtyard, lost in thought. It has been two years since that incident; no, perhaps it's only been two years.
[15] Two years ago, during the winter, three female students in Yutao's class were killed. The killing methods at the time could only be described as cruel, so the police initially suspected it was a revenge killing, but eventually corrected the course, turning it into a random, non-specific murder.
[16] The killer has not been apprehended.
[17] The girls' dormitory, which had been rumored to be closed, still remains in use. The victims' rooms should now be occupied by new students. Do these new students know about the murder of their predecessors in their living quarters? Or do they know but care little?
[18] Rui Dao sighed, his breath turning white. Perhaps he was thinking too much; he always felt that the student quality at Qinglian Academy had decreased significantly over the past two years. Of course, this was due to the continuous murders of female students.
[19] Even though the crime scene was in the girls' dormitory and had no direct connection to the male students, the male students would still hesitate to attend a school where a murder had occurred. It is likely that many students who originally planned to attend Qinglian changed their minds at the last minute. As a result, students who were not even on the waiting list were able to fill the vacancies and enroll...
[20] Rui Dao sighed again, his breath turning white. He told himself that he was thinking too much. However, when he thought about the fact that the girls' dormitory, which should have been closed, is still in use, he felt that his thoughts were reasonable.
[21] Qinglian Academy did not require students to live on campus, but first-year students were required to live on campus, and they could choose to leave after their second year. Therefore, female freshmen had to live on campus, regardless of the tragic incident that occurred there. Despite this, some students were willing to wear Qinglian's uniform—for students who had difficulty being admitted based on their original qualifications, this was a rare opportunity; after all, what harm could it do to live in a room where someone had died (male students had no such concerns)? If it were a single room, there might be some unease; but since the dorm rooms were all double-occupancy, there was nothing to fear… Students who took advantage of this situation to "turn a misfortune into a blessing" likely increased in number over the past two years.
[22] Yutao tried to remind himself not to think too much, but he couldn't help but dwell on the thought. This was a shared sentiment among all the staff members.
[23] Everyone was optimistic, believing that one day the situation would calm down. People's memories would fade, and even if they occasionally talked about the murders, they would forget whether they occurred in the boys' or girls' dormitories—such a moment would eventually arrive.
[24] In fact, only two years had passed, and the impact of the murders had already diminished significantly. Yutao himself felt this keenly.
[25] The abdomen he had glimpsed during his change of clothes reappeared in Yutao's mind. Over the past two years, Yutao had gained some weight. Partly because he got married soon after the incident and no longer had to manage all the household chores on his own; the increase in weight symbolized the stability of his life.
[26] The brutal murder case was just a dream, a mirage... Yitao soon fell into this illusion. He doesn't know what's going on in the world, but at least his surroundings are peaceful and secure - it's very easy to immerse oneself in this fantasy.
[27] In fact, Yitao has placed his mind and body in this "dream". Two years ago, he was still living alone in an apartment, but now he has built this over-sized house with the help of his wife's family.
[28] Yitao occasionally remembers or dreams about the case. Every time he thinks about it, the intensity of the murder case decreases, and the loose fat on his neck and abdomen increases in proportion.
[29] Now he can live his life as if nothing happened - or so he thinks. Not only Yitao, but the principal and the council should also have the same feeling. The nightmare is over. However...
[30] However, is that really the case? Yitao has a bitter and ironic sense of restlessness. Even if people's memories have faded, can everything go back to normal?
[31] For Wu Tai, whether the killer was caught or not didn't matter. Being left unresolved was also a form of closure. However, would everything be over for him, and would everything return to normal? Perhaps he would face the "consequences" next... This "feeling" drove him.
[32] It was this "feeling" that awakened him... Wu Tai couldn't help but think. This "feeling" forcefully pulled him out of the warm "dream" of the New Year.
[33] Without this "feeling", perhaps Wu Tai would have mistaken the scene in front of him for a dream. The temperature should have been much higher than midnight, but suddenly it started to snow.
[34] At first, the snowflakes were like dust, gradually turning into slowly flowing waterfalls; it was only then that Wu Tai realized that there was a dark figure standing by the entrance, unknown when it arrived.
[35] The feeling of intoxication similar to fear at that time was something Wu Tai would never forget.
[36] She, who is tall and thin, is wearing a black coat and has short waves in her hair that reaches her shoulders. The shadow is sharply defined against the snowy background that lulls one to sleep.
[37] Her eyes stare unblinkingly at Wutao, and the light from her slightly greenish whites almost swallows him. Suddenly, he feels his "death." He thinks he will freeze to death in her gaze. What a sweet way to die! He longs to fall asleep and never wake up... A painful desire drives Wutao, and he yearns to return to nothingness under her "illusion," buried in the pure "death."
[38] Wutao only later realizes that if he died at this time, he would be much happier.
[39] "I thought...," Wutao manages to speak, feeling as if he is dreaming and hearing someone else speak. "I thought I would never see you again."
[40] Wutao feels that his voice is absorbed by the veil of snowflakes, unsure if it reaches her ears. His knees fall to the ground at some point, and his lower body feels numb and powerless.
[41] "No, you…are you a phantom?" Wu Dao lay on the ground, kicking away the snow. "Are you really here? Not a phantom, a hallucination, or a dream? Please stay here, forever here—"
[42] Looking down at Wu Dao, her face was as white as snow, no, even whiter and colder. Wu Dao tried to get up, but his waist was powerless, and he could only stare at her legs that peeked out from under her coat.
[43] "Am I crazy? Is it my head that's messed up? Because I miss you so much—no, it's okay. As long as you…stay in front of me…"
[44] Wu Dao reached out his hand towards the black coat, trying to grab it to stand up, but his hands began to twitch, making it impossible for him to touch the coat and only grabbing and melting snowflakes.
[45] Wu Dao suddenly realized. His body was no longer fit to touch her, no longer worthy to stand in front of her; he was no longer beautiful, just a fat pig that dreamt every day. That was him. Was it…
[46] "You...you must hate me, right?" Wataru couldn't bear to look at her face anymore, so he lowered his gaze to her legs again. "But it's a misunderstanding. I've said it several times, but you don't seem to believe it, but it really is a misunderstanding. I didn't do anything to her, I swear."
[47] There was only silence from above. Wataru seemed to have broken free, grabbing her shoe tip and rubbing his forehead against it.
[48] "I am indeed a scumbag, a teacher who defiled a student and indulged in sinful pleasures. But I didn't, only her, only Hokuraku, I really didn't touch her, I swear. Believe me."
[49] If she would just kick my ugly face once, how refreshing... Wataru thought. However, she seemed to read his mind and made no reaction.
[50] "If only she would kick my ugly face once, how refreshing..." Wataru thought. However, she seemed to read his mind and made no reaction.
[51] How long did Tengdao lie in the snow? The blank silence, more empty than snow and colder than ice, exhausted Tengdao, and he slowly raised his vacant face. At this moment - her appearance changed.
[52] Her left hand was on her chest. Had she taken off her gloves or was she not wearing them to begin with? Her slender fingers drew a trajectory as white and fresh as snow on her black coat, but Tengdao did not understand the meaning of her posture.
[53] "Didn't you say you didn't touch Xiao Hui?"
[54] She - Takao Chiharu finally spoke. Hearing her voice, Tengdao felt relieved and had the leisure to observe Chiharu carefully.
[55] Tengdao originally thought that the only difference between Chiharu and the past was her hairstyle, but it was not the case; upon closer inspection, her appearance had changed a lot. Compared to the cold impression that seemed to touch electricity - no, even bleed when touched two years ago, she now appeared more peaceful, even more like a human.
[56] "Are you saying you didn't have a physical relationship with Xiao Hui? Or that you didn't kill her?"
[57] "What are you talking about? Of course, it's both! I and Kurokuma have never done anything inappropriate, and we haven't killed her. You know that, don't you?"
[58] Duo was startled. He stood up and brushed the fallen leaves that stuck to his face while crawling in the snow. He was ashamed of his crawling ugliness in front of her.
[59] "Of course, it's both! Kurokuma and I have never done anything inappropriate, and we haven't killed her. You know that, don't you?"
[60] Duo was greatly surprised.
[61] Because Sen gently smiled. She always had a blank expression, as if she was looking at a distant place; or else she would have laser-like eyes, as if she wanted to hit all the people who invaded her "domain". It was unexpected that she had the ability to smile.
[62] What happened to Sen? Do was jealous. Her smile was not for him, and her existence did not make her smile. Do knew it very well. Someone had changed her in the past two years, changed her like an ice pillar.
[63] "Did she have a man?" Do made a common guess, and couldn't help but smile bitterly. Sen was a woman who had no interest in men.
[64] "…You…" Do finally noticed that Sen's left hand was not wearing any jewelry. "Take off that ring…"
[65] "Yes." Sen seemed to be waiting for this sentence, hiding her fair left hand under her coat. "I have let go of Xiao Hui's matter."
[66] "Then…"
[67] "That's good…" Wu Dao didn't know if he should say this.

[93] ACT 1

[1712] Thousand Sails feels that she finally understands the meaning of Sugita Yongzi's warning to be careful. Thousand Sails does not think she is as beautiful as others describe, but unfortunately, she has to admit that the "danger" indicated by Yongzi indeed exists.
[1713] Simply put, normal interpersonal relationships can only be established by maintaining appropriate distance; it is a matter of course to respect the "individuality" of the other party.
[1714] However, in reality, humans rarely adhere to this matter-of-course "rule". People often violate the "individuality" of the other party in the name of love and prove their existence value by violating (or even allowing to be violated) it, even mistakenly believing that this is a proof of humanity. The most straightforward example is the parent-child relationship; parents consider invading the "personal domain" of their children as a matter of course or a duty, and regard fulfilling this duty as their mission.
[1715] This is not limited to the parent-child relationship. Friendship, love, marriage, neighborly, and workplace relationships - all can be applied. To put it in an extreme way, humans even mistakenly believe that love and friendship can only exist by violating the "individuality" of the other party; keeping an appropriate distance is often regarded as a cold and inconsiderate behavior.
[1716] This misunderstanding spreads because humans can find happiness in a state where their "individuality" is violated. Qianfan has this ability, and her relationship with Kubo Koumei is a perfect example. Koumei violated Qianfan's "individuality" and manipulated her personality for self-indulgence, and Qianfan enjoyed it because the object was Koumei.
[1717] As long as the "violator" and the "victim" have consistent interests, they can achieve a happy honeymoon. However, of course, the "victim" will also choose their object, not allowing anyone to violate them. The decision to accept or reject "violation" does not have absolute factors and can only be discovered through personal communication.
[1718] However, "violators" often do not consider these issues. On the contrary, they even unilaterally believe that their "violation" will make the other person happy. This is the case with parent-child relationships, and stalking crimes also have the same structure, always unilaterally believing that the other person's refusal of their love is "ungrateful."
[1719] Ultimately, all human relationships have the same structure. Asking others to maintain appropriate distance when interacting with them is a right that every individual should have; however, in reality, this claim is often seen as arrogant, often evaluated as self-important, and often ridiculed as self-righteous. In this, there is a jealous structure.
[1720] For humans, violating others' "individuality" is an undeniable pleasure; because for those who can "violate" others, it is a proof of "power" and a proof of existence value. Therefore, when faced with those who try to deprive them of this "pleasure," people become cunning and despicable. When a man sees a woman he cannot reach, he unjustly assumes that she is promiscuous or cold, which is a typical psychological response.
[1721] Once again, Chie does not think her appearance is beautiful; but she begins to feel that she may have some factors that can stimulate or trigger the universal desire of humans to violate others' "individuality." Sugata Yoshiko's "danger" may be in this sense.
[1722] In the face of "harmful intentions" around her, Chie has two ways to deal with herself. One is to completely accept "infringement" - as with her relationship with Kurokami Kei.
[1723] The other is to completely "reject" from the beginning, making it clear that she is not good at making friends or love. Even if this is done, there will still be people who try to approach Chie; but at least from the beginning, by clearly refusing, she can reduce her "degree of harm" to the minimum.
[1724] Humans are a species that always interprets others' words and actions as "signals that you can 'infringe' on me." Otherwise, how can a woman who only smiles politely be pursued and followed day and night by a man? Stalking crimes like this happen in reality because of this. Wanting to teach someone who is obedient is also due to the same structure.
[1725] To prevent this "misunderstanding" from happening, I must send clear signals of refusal at all times - this is the only decision Chie has made before entering university life. In conclusion, she will inevitably become "lonely." She does not intend to make friends, nor does she want to date, whether male or female; because no one can be like Kei, who allows her to reveal herself without any defense. So whether it is Ankoku University or other universities, the result is the same.
[1726] There is no third choice - there is no compromise option; even if Qianfan keeps a proper distance, it only gives others an opportunity to take advantage of her.

[2834] "Mukoda stuck the key under the mailbox without wearing gloves; it was difficult to tear the tape with gloves on. Kurokami might have revealed the key when questioned by the police, so he had to be careful not to leave fingerprints on it. However, the tape was difficult to tear, so he had to use his hands.
